<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> <a href="/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB" title="Pe̍h-ōe-jī">POJ</a></th>
<td>Mô͘ Te̍k-tong</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Mao Zedong</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Zh-Mao_Zedong.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:Zh-Mao_Zedong.ogg" title="File:Zh-Mao Zedong.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/aʊ/ 'ou' in 'pout'">aʊ</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'z' in 'Zion'">z</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ʊ/ short 'oo' in 'foot'">ʊ</span><span title="/ŋ/ 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="'z' in 'Zion'">z</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/-/ affix">-</span></span>/</a></span></span>), also <a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles" title="Wade–Giles">transliterated</a> as <b>Mao Tse-tung</b> and commonly referred to as <b>Chairman Mao</b> (December 26, 1893&#160;– September 9, 1976), was a <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communist</a> revolutionary and the <a href="/wiki/Founding_father" title="Founding father" class="mw-redirect">founding father</a> of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">People's Republic of China</a>, which he governed as <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Chairman of the Communist Party of China">Chairman of the Communist Party of China</a> from its establishment in 1949 until his death in 1976. His <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> theories, military strategies and political policies are collectively known as <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism%E2%80%93Maoism" title="Marxism–Leninism–Maoism">Marxism–Leninism–Maoism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Mao Zedong Thought</a>.</p>
<p>Born the son of a wealthy farmer in <a href="/wiki/Shaoshan" title="Shaoshan">Shaoshan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a>, Mao adopted a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_nationalism" title="Chinese nationalism">Chinese nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialist</a> outlook in early life, particularly influenced by the events of the <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> of 1911 and <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> of 1919. Mao converted to Marxism–Leninism while working at <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a> and became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> (CPC), leading the <a href="/wiki/Autumn_Harvest_Uprising" title="Autumn Harvest Uprising">Autumn Harvest Uprising</a> in 1927. During the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) and the CPC, Mao helped to found the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People.27s_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Red Army</a>, led the <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi_Soviet" title="Jiangxi Soviet" class="mw-redirect">Jiangxi Soviet</a>'s radical land policies and ultimately became head of the CPC during the <a href="/wiki/Long_March" title="Long March">Long March</a>. Although the CPC temporarily allied with the KMT under the <a href="/wiki/Second_United_Front" title="Second United Front">United Front</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937–45), after <a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day" title="Victory over Japan Day">Japan's defeat</a> China's civil war resumed and in 1949 Mao's forces defeated the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_government" title="Nationalist government">Nationalists</a> who withdrew to <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.</p>
<p>On October 1, 1949, Mao proclaimed the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC), a <a href="/wiki/Single-party_state" title="Single-party state">single-party state</a> controlled by the CPC. In the following years Mao solidified his control through <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">land reform</a> campaigns against landlords, and perceived enemies of the state he termed as "<a href="/wiki/Counter-revolutionaries" title="Counter-revolutionaries" class="mw-redirect">counter-revolutionaries</a>". In 1957 he launched a campaign known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> that aimed to rapidly transform China's economy from an <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_society" title="Agrarian society">agrarian</a> economy to an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_society" title="Industrial society">industrial</a> one, which led to a <a href="/wiki/Great_Chinese_Famine" title="Great Chinese Famine">widespread famine</a> whose death toll is estimated at between 18 and 45 million. In 1966, he initiated the <a href="/wiki/Great_Proletarian_Cultural_Revolution" title="Great Proletarian Cultural Revolution" class="mw-redirect">Great Proletarian Cultural Revolution</a>, a program to remove "<a href="/wiki/Counter-revolutionary" title="Counter-revolutionary">counter-revolutionary</a>" elements of Chinese society that lasted 10 years and which was marked by violent class struggle, widespread destruction of cultural artifacts and unprecedented elevation of Mao's <a href="/wiki/Personality_cult" title="Personality cult" class="mw-redirect">personality cult</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1972, Mao <a href="/wiki/1972_Nixon_visit_to_China" title="1972 Nixon visit to China">welcomed US president Richard Nixon</a> in Beijing, signalling <a href="/wiki/Open_Door_Policy#In_modern_China" title="Open Door Policy">a policy of opening China</a>, which was furthered under <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a>'s rule in China.</p>
<p>A controversial figure, Mao is regarded as one of the most important individuals in modern world history.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Supporters credit him with driving <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a> out of China,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> modernising China and building it into a <a href="/wiki/World_power" title="World power" class="mw-redirect">world power</a>, promoting the status of women, improving education and health care, and increasing <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> as China's population grew from around 550 to over 900 million during the period of his leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-China_2010.2C_pp._327_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China_2010.2C_pp._327-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> He is also known as a theorist, military strategist, poet, and visionary.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In contrast, critics consider him a <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a> who severely damaged traditional Chinese culture, as well as a perpetrator of systematic <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_abuse" title="Human rights abuse" class="mw-redirect">human rights abuses</a> who was responsible for an estimated 40 to 70 million deaths through starvation, <a href="/wiki/Laogai" title="Laogai">forced labour</a> and executions, ranking his tenure as the top incidence of <a href="/wiki/Democide" title="Democide">democide</a> in human history.<sup id="cite_ref-deathtoll_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deathtoll-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fenby_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fenby-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_life_of_Mao_Zedong" title="Early life of Mao Zedong">Early life of Mao Zedong</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_and_the_Xinhai_Revolution:_1893.E2.80.931911">Youth and the Xinhai Revolution: 1893–1911</span></h3>
<p>Mao Zedong was born on December 26, 1893 in <a href="/wiki/Shaoshan" title="Shaoshan">Shaoshan</a> village, <a href="/wiki/Hunan_Province" title="Hunan Province" class="mw-redirect">Hunan Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram196619Hollingworth198515PantsovLevine201211_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram196619Hollingworth198515PantsovLevine201211-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> His father, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Yichang" title="Mao Yichang">Mao Yichang</a>, was an impoverished peasant who had become one of the wealthiest farmers in Shaoshan. Growing up in rural Hunan, Mao Zedong described his father as a stern disciplinarian, who would beat him and his three siblings, the boys <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zemin" title="Mao Zemin">Zemin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zetan" title="Mao Zetan">Zetan</a>, and an adopted girl, Zejian.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao's mother, <a href="/wiki/Wen_Qimei" title="Wen Qimei">Wen Qimei</a>, was a devout <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> who tried to temper her husband's strict attitude.<sup id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Zedong too became a Buddhist, but abandoned this faith in his mid-teenage years.<sup id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> At age 8, Mao was sent to Shaoshan Primary School. Learning the value systems of <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, he later admitted that he didn't enjoy the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_classics" title="Chinese classics">classical Chinese texts</a> preaching Confucian morals, instead favouring popular novels like <i><a href="/wiki/Romance_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" title="Romance of the Three Kingdoms">Romance of the Three Kingdoms</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Water_Margin" title="Water Margin">Water Margin</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> At age 13, Mao finished primary education, and his father <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">had him married</a> to the 17-year-old <a href="/wiki/Luo_Yigu" title="Luo Yigu" class="mw-redirect">Luo Yigu</a>, uniting their land-owning families. Mao refused to recognise her as his wife, becoming a fierce critic of arranged marriage and temporarily moving away. Luo was locally disgraced and died in 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shaoshan_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shaoshan_01.JPG/220px-Shaoshan_01.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shaoshan_01.JPG/330px-Shaoshan_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shaoshan_01.JPG/440px-Shaoshan_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3328" data-file-height="1872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shaoshan_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong%27s_Former_Residence" title="Mao Zedong's Former Residence">Mao's childhood home</a> in Shaoshan, in 2010, by which time it had become a tourist destination.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Working on his father's farm, Mao read voraciously,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> developing a "political consciousness" from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zheng_Guanying&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zheng Guanying (page does not exist)">Zheng Guanying</a>'s booklet which lamented the deterioration of Chinese power and argued for the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Interested in history, Mao was inspired by the military prowess and nationalistic fervour of <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect">Napoleon Bonaparte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> His political views were shaped by <a href="/wiki/Gelaohui" title="Gelaohui">Gelaohui</a>-led protests which erupted following a famine in Hunanese capital <a href="/wiki/Changsha" title="Changsha">Changsha</a>; Mao supported the protesters' demands, but the armed forces suppressed the dissenters and executed their leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The famine spread to Shaoshan, where starving peasants seized his father's grain; disapproving of their actions as morally wrong, Mao nevertheless claimed sympathy for their situation.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> At age 16, Mao moved to a higher primary school in nearby Dongshan,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> where he was bullied for his peasant background.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1911, Mao began middle school in Changsha.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Revolutionary sentiment was strong in the city, with widespread animosity towards Emperor <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">Puyi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> and many advocating <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a>. The republicans' figurehead was <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a>, an American-educated Christian who led the <a href="/wiki/Tongmenghui" title="Tongmenghui">Tongmenghui</a> society.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> In Changsha, Mao was influenced by Sun's newspaper, <i>The People's Independence</i> (<i>Minli bao</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> and called for Sun to become president in a school essay.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> As a symbol of rebellion against the <a href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu" class="mw-redirect">Manchu</a> monarch, Mao and a friend cut off their <a href="/wiki/Queue_(hairstyle)" title="Queue (hairstyle)">queue</a> pigtails, a sign of subservience to the emperor.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Inspired by Sun's republicanism, the army rose up across southern China, sparking the <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a>. Changsha's governor fled, leaving the city in republican control.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Supporting the revolution, Mao joined the rebel army as a <a href="/wiki/Private_soldier" title="Private soldier" class="mw-redirect">private soldier</a>, but was not involved in fighting. The northern provinces remained loyal to the emperor, and hoping to avoid a civil war, Sun—proclaimed "provisional president" by his supporters—compromised with the monarchist general <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a>. The monarchy would be abolished, creating the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)" class="mw-redirect">Republic of China</a>, but the monarchist Yuan would become president. The revolution over, Mao resigned from the army in 1912, after six months of being a soldier.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Around this time, Mao discovered <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> from a newspaper article; proceeding to read pamphlets by <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Kanghu" title="Jiang Kanghu">Jiang Kanghu</a>, the student founder of the Chinese Socialist Party, Mao remained interested yet unconvinced by the idea.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_Normal_School_of_Changsha:_1912.E2.80.9319">Fourth Normal School of Changsha: 1912–19</span></h3>
<p>Over the next few years, Mao enrolled and dropped out of a police academy, a soap-production school, a law school, an economics school, and the government-run Changsha Middle School.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Studying independently, he spent much time in Changsha's library, reading core works of <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberalism</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wealth_of_Nations" title="The Wealth of Nations">The Wealth of Nations</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Montesquieu" title="Montesquieu">Montesquieu</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spirit_of_the_Laws" title="The Spirit of the Laws">The Spirit of the Laws</a></i>, as well as the works of western scientists and philosophers such as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Darwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rousseau" title="Rousseau" class="mw-redirect">Rousseau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Spencer" title="Herbert Spencer">Spencer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Viewing himself as an intellectual, years later he admitted that at this time he thought himself better than working people.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Inspired by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Paulsen" title="Friedrich Paulsen">Friedrich Paulsen</a>, the liberal emphasis on individualism led Mao to believe that strong individuals were not bound by moral codes but should strive for the greater good; that the <a href="/wiki/Consequentialism" title="Consequentialism">end justifies the means</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Seeing no use in his son's intellectual pursuits, Mao's father cut off his allowance, forcing him to move into a hostel for the destitute.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg/170px-Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg/255px-Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg/340px-Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg 2x" data-file-width="395" data-file-height="520" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mao in 1913</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Desiring to become a teacher, Mao enrolled at the Fourth Normal School of Changsha, which soon merged with the First Normal School of Changsha, widely seen as the best school in Hunan.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Befriending Mao, professor <a href="/wiki/Yang_Changji" title="Yang Changji">Yang Changji</a> urged him to read a radical newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/La_Jeunesse" title="La Jeunesse" class="mw-redirect">New Youth</a></i> (<i>Xin qingnian</i>), the creation of his friend <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a>, a dean at <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>. Although a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_nationalism" title="Chinese nationalism">Chinese nationalist</a>, Chen argued that China must look to the west to cleanse itself of superstition and autocracy.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao published his first article in <i>New Youth</i> in April 1917, instructing readers to increase their physical strength to serve the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> He joined the Society for the Study of Wang Fuzhi (<i>Chuan-shan Hsüeh-she</i>), a revolutionary group founded by Changsha literati who wished to emulate the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Wang_Fuzhi" title="Wang Fuzhi">Wang Fuzhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In his first school year, Mao befriended an older student, <a href="/wiki/Xiao_Zisheng" title="Xiao Zisheng">Xiao Zisheng</a>; together they went on a walking tour of Hunan, begging and writing literary couplets to obtain food.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> A popular student, in 1915 Mao was elected secretary of the Students Society. Forging an Association for Student Self-Government, he led protests against school rules.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In spring 1917, he was elected to command the students' volunteer army, set up to defend the school from marauding soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Increasingly interested in the techniques of war, he took a keen interest in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and also began to develop a sense of solidarity with workers.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao undertook feats of physical endurance with Xiao Zisheng and <a href="/wiki/Cai_Hesen" title="Cai Hesen">Cai Hesen</a>, and with other young revolutionaries they formed the Renovation of the People Study Society in April 1918 to debate Chen Duxiu's ideas. Desiring personal and societal transformation, the Society gained 70–80 members, many of whom would later join the Communist Party.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao graduated in June 1919, being ranked third in the year.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Revolutionary_Activity">Early Revolutionary Activity</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_revolutionary_activity_of_Mao_Zedong" title="Early revolutionary activity of Mao Zedong">Early revolutionary activity of Mao Zedong</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beijing.2C_Anarchism.2C_and_Marxism:_1917.E2.80.9319">Beijing, Anarchism, and Marxism: 1917–19</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:278px;max-width:278px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Marx6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Marx6.jpg/130px-Marx6.jpg" width="130" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Marx6.jpg/195px-Marx6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Marx6.jpg/260px-Marx6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="345" data-file-height="504" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Lenin_140-190_for_collage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Vladimir_Lenin_140-190_for_collage.jpg" width="140" height="190" data-file-width="140" data-file-height="190" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Following the success of the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> in the former Russian Empire, in which Marxists took power, Mao came under the theoretical influence of <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> (right).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mao moved to <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, where his mentor Yang Changji had taken a job at Peking University.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Yang thought Mao exceptionally "intelligent and handsome",<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> securing him a job as assistant to the university librarian <a href="/wiki/Li_Dazhao" title="Li Dazhao">Li Dazhao</a>, an early Chinese Communist.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Li authored a series of <i>New Youth</i> articles on the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> in Russia, during which the Communist <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik_Party" title="Bolshevik Party" class="mw-redirect">Bolshevik Party</a> under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> had seized power. Lenin was an advocate of the socio-political theory of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a>, first developed by the German sociologists <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">Friedrich Engels</a>, and Li's articles brought an understanding of Marxism to the Chinese revolutionary movement.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Becoming "more and more radical", Mao was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a> but joined Li's Study Group and "developed rapidly toward Marxism" during the winter of 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Paid a low wage, Mao lived in a cramped room with seven other Hunanese students, but believed that Beijing's beauty offered "vivid and living compensation".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> At the university, Mao was widely snubbed by other students due to his rural Hunanese accent and lowly position. By joining the university's Philosophy and Journalism Societies, he attended lectures and seminars by the likes of <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hu_Shi" title="Hu Shi" class="mw-redirect">Hu Shi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qian_Xuantong" title="Qian Xuantong">Qian Xuantong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao's time in Beijing ended in the spring of 1919, when he travelled to <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> with friends departing for France,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> before returning to Shaoshan, where his mother was terminally ill; she died in October 1919, with her husband dying in January 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Culture_and_political_protests.2C_1919.E2.80.9320">New Culture and political protests, 1919–20</span></h3>
<p>On May 4, 1919, students in Beijing gathered at the Gate of Heavenly Peace to protest the Chinese government's weak resistance to Japanese expansion in China. Patriots had been outraged at the influence given to Japan in the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-One_Demands" title="Twenty-One Demands">Twenty-One Demands</a> in 1915, the complicity of <a href="/wiki/Duan_Qirui" title="Duan Qirui">Duan Qirui</a>’s <a href="/wiki/Beiyang_Government" title="Beiyang Government" class="mw-redirect">Beiyang Government</a>, and the betrayal of China at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> by allowing Japan to <a href="/wiki/Shandong_Problem" title="Shandong Problem">receive territories in Shandong</a> which had been surrendered by <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>. These demonstrations ignited the nation-wide <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> and fueled the <a href="/wiki/New_Culture_Movement" title="New Culture Movement">New Culture Movement</a> which blamed China’s diplomatic defeats on social and cultural backwardness.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Changsha, Mao had begun teaching history at the Xiuye Primary School<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> and organizing protests against the pro-Duan Governor of Hunan Province, <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Jingyao" title="Zhang Jingyao">Zhang Jingyao</a>, popularly known as "Zhang the Venomous" due to his corrupt and violent rule.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> In late May, Mao co-founded the Hunanese Student Association with <a href="/wiki/He_Shuheng" title="He Shuheng">He Shuheng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deng_Zhongxia" title="Deng Zhongxia">Deng Zhongxia</a>, organizing a student strike for June and in July 1919 began production of a weekly radical magazine, <i>Xiang River Review</i> (<i>Xiangjiang pinglun</i>). Using vernacular language that would be understandable to the majority of China's populace, he advocated the need for a "Great Union of the Popular Masses", strengthened trade unions able to wage non-violent revolution; his ideas were not Marxist, but heavily influenced by Kropotkin's concept of <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Aid:_A_Factor_of_Evolution" title="Mutual Aid: A Factor of Evolution">mutual aid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_(May_4,_1919).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/220px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/330px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/440px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="485" data-file-height="336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_(May_4,_1919).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students in Beijing rallied during the May Fourth Movement.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Zhang banned the Student Association, but Mao continued publishing after assuming editorship of liberal magazine <i>New Hunan</i> (<i>Xin Hunan</i>) and offering articles in popular local newspaper <i>Justice</i> (<i>Ta Kung Po</i>). Several of these articles advocated <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminist</a> views, calling for the liberation of women in Chinese society; Mao was influenced by his forced arranged-marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1919, Mao helped organise a general strike in Hunan, securing some concessions, but Mao and other student leaders felt threatened by Zhang, and Mao returned to Beijing, visiting the terminally ill Yang Changji.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao found that his articles had achieved a level of fame among the revolutionary movement, and set about soliciting support in overthrowing Zhang.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Coming across newly translated Marxist literature by Thomas Kirkup, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Kautsky" title="Karl Kautsky">Karl Kautsky</a>, and Marx and Engels—notably <i><a href="/wiki/The_Communist_Manifesto" title="The Communist Manifesto">The Communist Manifesto</a></i>—he came under their increasing influence, but was still eclectic in his views.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Mao visited Tianjin, <a href="/wiki/Jinan" title="Jinan">Jinan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qufu" title="Qufu">Qufu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> before moving to Shanghai, where he worked as a laundryman and met <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a>, noting that Chen's adoption of Marxism "deeply impressed me at what was probably a critical period in my life". In Shanghai, Mao met an old teacher of his, <a href="/wiki/Yi_Peiji" title="Yi Peiji">Yi Peiji</a>, a revolutionary and member of the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT), or Chinese Nationalist Party, which was gaining increasing support and influence. Yi introduced Mao to General <a href="/wiki/Tan_Yankai" title="Tan Yankai">Tan Yankai</a>, a senior KMT member who held the loyalty of troops stationed along the Hunanese border with Guangdong. Tan was plotting to overthrow Zhang, and Mao aided him by organizing the Changsha students. In June 1920, Tan led his troops into Changsha, while Zhang fled. In the subsequent reorganization of the provincial administration, Mao was appointed headmaster of the junior section of the First Normal School. Now receiving a large income, he married Yang Kaihui in the winter of 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_the_Communist_Party_of_China:_1921.E2.80.9322">Founding the Communist Party of China: 1921–22</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg/170px-Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg/255px-Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg/340px-Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1706" data-file-height="2385" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Location of the first Congress of the Chinese Communist Party in July 1921, in <a href="/wiki/Xintiandi" title="Xintiandi">Xintiandi</a>, former <a href="/wiki/French_Concession" title="French Concession" class="mw-redirect">French Concession</a>, Shanghai.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> was founded by Chen Duxiu and <a href="/wiki/Li_Dazhao" title="Li Dazhao">Li Dazhao</a> in the <a href="/wiki/French_concession" title="French concession" class="mw-redirect">French concession</a> of Shanghai in 1921 as a study society and informal network. Mao set up a Changsha branch, also establishing a branch of the Socialist Youth Corps. Opening a bookstore under the control of his new Cultural Book Society, its purpose was to propagate revolutionary literature throughout Hunan.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Helping to organise workers' strikes in the winter of 1920–21,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> he was involved in the movement for Hunan autonomy, hoping that a Hunanese constitution would increase <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberty" title="Civil liberty" class="mw-redirect">civil liberties</a> in the province, making his revolutionary activity easier; although the movement was successful, in later life, he denied any involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1921, small Marxist groups existed in Shanghai, Beijing, Changsha, Wuhan, Canton and Jinan, and it was decided to hold a central meeting, which began in Shanghai on July 23, 1921. The first session of the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="National Congress of the Communist Party of China">National Congress of the Communist Party of China</a> was attended by 13 delegates, Mao included, and met in a girls' school that was closed for the summer. After the authorities sent a police spy to the congress, the delegates moved to a boat on South Lake near Chiahsing to escape detection. Although Soviet and <a href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern" class="mw-redirect">Comintern</a> delegates attended, the first congress ignored Lenin's advice to accept a temporary alliance between the Communists and the "bourgeois democrats" who also advocated national revolution; instead they stuck to the orthodox Marxist belief that only the urban proletariat could lead a socialist revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Now party secretary for Hunan, Mao was stationed in Changsha, from which he went on a Communist recruitment drive.<sup id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p68_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p68-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 1921, he founded the Self-Study University, through which readers could gain access to revolutionary literature, housed in the premises of the Society for the Study of Wang Fuzhi.<sup id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p68_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p68-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Taking part in the <a href="/wiki/Y.C._James_Yen#Biography" title="Y.C. James Yen" class="mw-redirect">YMCA</a> mass education movement to fight illiteracy, he opened a Changsha branch, though replaced the usual textbooks with revolutionary tracts in order to spread Marxism among the students.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> He continued organizing the labour movement to strike against the administration of Hunan Governor <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Hengti" title="Zhao Hengti">Zhao Hengti</a>, particularly following the execution of two anarchists.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In July 1922, the Second Congress of the Communist Party took place in Shanghai, though Mao lost the address and couldn't attend. Adopting Lenin's advice, the delegates agreed to an alliance with the "bourgeois democrats" of the KMT for the good of the "national revolution". Communist Party members joined the KMT, hoping to push its politics leftward.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao enthusiastically agreed with this decision, arguing for an alliance across China's socio-economic classes; a vocal anti-imperialist, in his writings he lambasted the governments of Japan, UK and US, describing the latter as "the most murderous of hangmen".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao's strategy for the successful and famous <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anyuan_Coal_Mine_Strike&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anyuan Coal Mine Strike (page does not exist)">Anyuan coal mines strikes</a> (contrary to later Party historians) depended on both "proletarian" and "bourgeois" strategies. The success depended on innovative organizing by Liu Shaoqi and Li Lisan who not only mobilised the miners, but formed schools and cooperatives. They also engaged local intellectuals, gentry, military officers, merchants, Red Gang dragon heads and church clergy in support.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaboration_with_the_Kuomintang:_1922.E2.80.9327">Collaboration with the Kuomintang: 1922–27</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao1927.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Mao1927.jpg/170px-Mao1927.jpg" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Mao1927.jpg/255px-Mao1927.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Mao1927.jpg/340px-Mao1927.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="594" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao1927.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mao the revolutionary in 1927.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the Third Congress of the Communist Party in Shanghai in June 1923, the delegates reaffirmed their commitment to working with the KMT against the Beiyang government and imperialists. Supporting this position, Mao was elected to the Party Committee, taking up residence in Shanghai. <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Attending the First KMT Congress, held in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> in early 1924, Mao was elected an alternate member of the KMT Central Executive Committee, and put forward four resolutions to decentralise power to urban and rural bureaus. His enthusiastic support for the KMT earned him the suspicion of some Communists.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> In late 1924, Mao returned to Shaoshan to recuperate from an illness. Discovering that the peasantry were increasingly restless due to the upheaval of the past decade, some had seized land from wealthy landowners to found communes; this convinced him of the revolutionary potential of the peasantry, an idea advocated by the KMT but not the Communists.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, he was appointed to run the KMT's <a href="/wiki/Peasant_Movement_Training_Institute_at_Guangzhou" title="Peasant Movement Training Institute at Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect">Peasant Movement Training Institute</a>, also becoming Director of its Propaganda Department and editing its <i>Political Weekly</i> (<i>Zhengzhi zhoubao</i>) newsletter.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_36_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_36-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Through the Peasant Movement Training Institute, Mao took an active role in organizing the revolutionary Hunanese peasants and preparing them for militant activity, taking them through military training exercises and getting them to study various left-wing texts.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In the winter of 1925, Mao fled to <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a> after his revolutionary activities attracted the attention of Zhao's regional authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Communists controlled the left wing of the KMT, struggling for power with the party's right wing. When party leader Sun Yat-sen died in May 1925, he was succeeded by a rightist, <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, who initiated moves to marginalise the position of the Communists.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao nevertheless supported Chiang's decision to overthrow the Beiyang government and their foreign imperialist allies using the <a href="/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army" title="National Revolutionary Army">National Revolutionary Army</a>, who embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">Northern Expedition</a> in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> In the wake of this expedition, peasants rose up, appropriating the land of the wealthy landowners, whom were in many cases killed. Such uprisings angered senior KMT figures, who were themselves landowners, emphasizing the growing class and ideological divide within the revolutionary movement.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #ACE1AF;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Revolution is not a dinner party, nor an essay, nor a painting, nor a piece of embroidery; it cannot be so refined, so leisurely and gentle, so temperate, kind, courteous, restrained and magnanimous. A revolution is an insurrection, an act of violence by which one class overthrows another."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>— Mao, February 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>In March 1927, Mao appeared at the Third Plenum of the KMT Central Executive Committee in Wuhan, which sought to strip General Chiang of his power by appointing <a href="/wiki/Wang_Jingwei" title="Wang Jingwei">Wang Jingwei</a> leader. There, Mao played an active role in the discussions regarding the peasant issue, defending a set of "Regulations for the Repression of Local Bullies and Bad Gentry", which advocated the death penalty or life imprisonment for anyone found guilty of <a href="/wiki/Counter-revolution" title="Counter-revolution" class="mw-redirect">counter-revolutionary</a> activity, arguing that in a revolutionary situation, "peaceful methods cannot suffice".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_42_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_42-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 1927, Mao was appointed to the KMT's five-member Central Land Committee, urging peasants to refuse to pay rent. Mao led another group to put together a "Draft Resolution on the Land Question", which called for the confiscation of land belonging to "local bullies and bad gentry, corrupt officials, militarists and all counter-revolutionary elements in the villages". Proceeding to carry out a "Land Survey", he stated that anyone owning over 30 <i>mou</i> (four and a half acres), constituting 13% of the population, were uniformly counter-revolutionary. He accepted that there was great variation in revolutionary enthusiasm across the country, and that a flexible policy of land redistribution was necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Presenting his conclusions at the Enlarged Land Committee meeting, many expressed reservations, some believing that it went too far, and others not far enough. Ultimately, his suggestions were only partially implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Revolution_(1949)" title="Chinese Revolution (1949)" class="mw-redirect">Chinese Revolution (1949)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Nanchang_and_Autumn_Harvest_Uprisings:_1927">The Nanchang and Autumn Harvest Uprisings: 1927</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/220px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/330px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/440px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="229" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People.27s_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fresh from the success of the Northern Expedition to overthrow the warlords, Chiang turned on the Communists, who by now numbered in the tens of thousands across China. Ignoring the orders of the Wuhan-based KMT government, he marched on Shanghai, a city controlled by Communist militias. Although the Communists welcomed Chiang's arrival, he turned on them, massacring 5000 with the aid of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Gang" title="Green Gang">Green Gang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_42_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_42-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Chiang's army then marched on Wuhan, but was prevented from taking the city by Communist General <a href="/wiki/Ye_Ting" title="Ye Ting">Ye Ting</a> and his troops.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Chiang's allies also attacked Communists; in Beijing, 19 leading Communists were killed by <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zuolin" title="Zhang Zuolin">Zhang Zuolin</a>, while in Changsha, He Jian's forces machine gunned hundreds of peasant militiamen.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p62_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p62-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> That May, tens of thousands of Communists and their sympathisers were killed by nationalists, with the CPC losing approximately 15,000 of its 25,000 members.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p62_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p62-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:15em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #ACE1AF;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"'Eagles cleave the air,<br />
Fish glide in the limpid deep;<br />
Under freezing skies a million<br />
creatures contend in freedom.<br />
Brooding over this immensity,<br />
I ask, on this boundless land<br />
Who rules over man's destiny?"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>— Excerpt from Mao's<br />
poem "Changsha", September 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p64_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p64-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>The CPC continued supporting the Wuhan KMT government, a position Mao initially supported,<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p62_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p62-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> but he had changed his mind by the time of the CPC's Fifth Congress, deciding to stake all hope on the peasant militia.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p63_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p63-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> The question was rendered moot when the Wuhan government expelled all Communists from the KMT on July 15.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p63_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p63-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC founded the Workers' and Peasants' Red Army of China, better known as the "<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People.27s_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Red Army</a>", to battle Chiang. A battalion led by General <a href="/wiki/Zhu_De" title="Zhu De">Zhu De</a> was ordered to take the city of <a href="/wiki/Nanchang" title="Nanchang">Nanchang</a> on August 1, 1927 in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Nanchang_Uprising" title="Nanchang Uprising">Nanchang Uprising</a>; initially successful, they were forced into retreat after five days, marching south to <a href="/wiki/Shantou" title="Shantou">Shantou</a>, and from there being driven into the wilderness of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p63_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p63-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Appointed commander-in-chief of the Red Army, Mao led four regiments against Changsha in the <a href="/wiki/Autumn_Harvest_Uprising" title="Autumn Harvest Uprising">Autumn Harvest Uprising</a>, hoping to spark peasant uprisings across Hunan. On the eve of the attack, Mao composed a poem—the earliest of his to survive—titled "Changsha". His plan was to attack the KMT-held city from three directions on September 9, but the Fourth Regiment deserted to the KMT cause, attacking the Third Regiment. Mao's army made it to Changsha, but could not take it; by September 15, he accepted defeat, with 1000 survivors marching east to the <a href="/wiki/Jinggang_Mountains" title="Jinggang Mountains">Jinggang Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p64_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p64-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In their biography of Mao, <i><a href="/wiki/Mao:_The_Unknown_Story" title="Mao: The Unknown Story">Mao: The Unknown Story</a></i>, Jung Chang and Jon Halliday dispute this version of events.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Chang and Halliday claim that the uprising was in fact sabotaged by Mao to allow him to snare a force of Nationalist mutineers from Nanchang who were crossing over to the CPC, prevent them from defecting to any other CPC leader, and enhance his own personal power within the CPC. They claim that Mao's three-day delay in seeing the other leaders of the Hunan uprising, scheduled for August 15 but delayed by Mao until August 18, was to allow Mao to check that the mutineers would still be passing close by and that if Mao had not had the opportunity of adding this force to his own forces within the CPC he would not have gone to south Hunan.<sup id="cite_ref-ChangHalliday_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChangHalliday-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chang and Halliday also claim that Mao lobbied to narrow down the uprising and talked the other leaders (including Russian diplomats at the Soviet consulate in Changsha who, Chang and Halliday claim, had been controlling much of the CPC activity) into striking only at Changsha. This, they say, was in order to allow Mao to also gain control of a force of 1,700 peasant rebels and defectors from the Nationalist army who were near Changsha. Chang and Halliday point out that once Mao had gained control of these men, he then moved to a position 100&#160;km east of Changsha at Wenjiashi and was there on September 11, the uprising's launch date, far from his troops, and that on September 14, before the troops had reached Changsha or met heavy resistance, Mao ordered them to abandon the assault on Changsha and converge on his position. Chang and Halliday report a view sent to Moscow by the secretary of the Soviet Consulate in Changsha that the retreat was "the most despicable treachery and cowardice."<sup id="cite_ref-ChangHalliday_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChangHalliday-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chang and Halliday allege that Mao later fabricated the version of events in order to hide the fact that far from leading a peasant uprising, he hijacked it for his own personal ends, sabotaged the organisation, and departed with the new troops before the attack on Changsha had begun.<sup id="cite_ref-ChangHalliday_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChangHalliday-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Base_in_Jinggangshan:_1927.E2.80.931928">Base in Jinggangshan: 1927–1928</span></h3>
<p>Hiding in Shanghai, the CPC Central Committee expelled Mao from their ranks and from the Hunan Provincial Committee, punishment for his "military opportunism", for his focus on rural activity, and for being too lenient with "bad gentry". They nevertheless adopted three policies he had long championed: the immediate formation of <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_council" title="Workers' council">Workers' councils</a>, the confiscation of all land without exemption, and the rejection of the KMT. Mao's response was to ignore them.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Setting up base in <a href="/wiki/Jinggangshan_City" title="Jinggangshan City">Jinggangshan City</a>, an area of the Jinggang Mountains, Mao united five villages as a self-governing state, supporting the confiscation of land from rich landlords, who were "re-educated" and sometimes executed. He ensured that no massacres took place in the region, pursuing a more lenient approach than that advocated by the Central Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Proclaiming that "Even the lame, the deaf and the blind could all come in useful for the revolutionary struggle", he boosted the army's numbers,<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p69_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p69-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> incorporating two groups of bandits into his army, building a force of around 1,800 troops.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> He laid down rules for his soldiers: prompt obedience to orders, all confiscations were to be turned over to the government, and nothing was to be confiscated from poorer peasants. In doing so, he molded his men into a disciplined, efficient fighting force.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p69_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p69-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:20em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #ACE1AF;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"When the enemy advances, we retreat.<br />
When the enemy rests, we harass him.<br />
When the enemy avoids a battle, we attack.<br />
When the enemy retreats, we advance."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>Mao's advice in combating the Kuomintang, 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p70_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p70-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>In spring 1928, the Central Committee ordered Mao's troops to southern Hunan, hoping to spark peasant uprisings. Mao was skeptical, but complied. Reaching Hunan, they were attacked by the KMT and fled after heavy losses. Meanwhile, KMT troops had invaded Jinggangshan, leaving them without a base.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Wandering the countryside, Mao's forces came across a CPC regiment led by General <a href="/wiki/Zhu_De" title="Zhu De">Zhu De</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lin_Biao" title="Lin Biao">Lin Biao</a>; they united, attempting to retake Jinggangshan. Initially successful, the KMT counter-attacked, pushing the CPC back; over the next few weeks, they fought an entrenched guerrilla war in the mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p70_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p70-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Central Committee again ordered Mao to march to south Hunan, but he refused, remaining at his base. Contrastingly, Zhu complied, leading his armies away; the KMT attacked Mao's base, and although his troops fended them off for 25 days, Mao left the camp at night to find reinforcements. Reuniting with the decimated Zhu's army, they returned to Jinggangshan and retook the base. Joined by a defecting KMT regiment and <a href="/wiki/Peng_Dehuai" title="Peng Dehuai">Peng Dehuai</a>'s Fifth Red Army, the mountainous area was unable to grow enough crops to feed everyone, leading to food shortages throughout the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_50_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_50-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jiangxi_Soviet_Republic_of_China:_1929.E2.80.931934">Jiangxi Soviet Republic of China: 1929–1934</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg/220px-1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg/330px-1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a8/1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="285" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1928_Mao_and_third_wife_He_Jijen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mao with his third wife, <a href="/wiki/He_Zizhen" title="He Zizhen">He Zizhen</a>, 1928</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 1929, Mao and Zhu evacuated the base and took their armies south, to the area around <a href="/wiki/Tonggu_County" title="Tonggu County">Tonggu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xinfeng_County,_Jiangxi" title="Xinfeng County, Jiangxi">Xinfeng</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a>, which they consolidated as a new base.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Together having 2,000 men, with a further 800 provided by Peng, the evacuation led to a drop in morale, and many troops became disobedient and began thieving; this worried <a href="/wiki/Li_Lisan" title="Li Lisan">Li Lisan</a> and the Central Committee, who saw Mao's army as <i><a href="/wiki/Lumpenproletariat" title="Lumpenproletariat">lumpenproletariat</a></i>, unable to share in proletariat <a href="/wiki/Class_consciousness" title="Class consciousness">class consciousness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p72_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p72-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> In keeping with orthodox Marxist thought, Li believed that only the urban proletariat could lead a successful revolution, and saw little need for Mao's peasant guerrillas; he ordered Mao to disband his army into units to be sent out to spread the revolutionary message. Mao replied that while concurring with Li's theoretical position, he would not disband his army or abandon his base.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p72_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p72-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Both Li and Mao saw the Chinese revolution as the key to <a href="/wiki/World_revolution" title="World revolution">world revolution</a>, believing that a CPC victory would spark the overthrow of global imperialism and capitalism. In this, they disagreed with the official line of the Soviet government and Comintern. Officials in Moscow desired greater control over the CPC, removing Li from power by calling him to Russia for an inquest into his errors.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p75_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p75-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_51_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_51-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> They replaced him with Soviet-educated Chinese Communists, known as the "<a href="/wiki/28_Bolsheviks" title="28 Bolsheviks">28 Bolsheviks</a>", two of whom, <a href="/wiki/Bo_Gu" title="Bo Gu">Bo Gu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Wentian" title="Zhang Wentian">Zhang Wentian</a>, took control of the Central Committee. Mao disagreed with the new leadership, believing they grasped little of the Chinese situation, and soon emerged as their key rival.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p75_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p75-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1930, Mao created the Southwest Jiangxi Provincial Soviet Government in the region under his control,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> in November suffering emotional trauma after his wife and sister were captured and beheaded by KMT general He Jian.<sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_50_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_50-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p75_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p75-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p153_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p153-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> He then married <a href="/wiki/He_Zizhen" title="He Zizhen">He Zizhen</a>, an 18-year-old revolutionary who bore him five children over the following nine years.<sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_51_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_51-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schram_p208_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schram_p208-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Facing internal problems, members of the Jiangxi Soviet accused him of being too moderate, and hence anti-revolutionary. In December, they tried to overthrow Mao, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Futian_incident" title="Futian incident">Futian incident</a>; putting down the rebels, Mao's loyalists tortured many and executed between 2000 and 3000 dissenters.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p76_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p76-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Seeing it as a secure area, the CPC Central Committee moved to Jiangxi, which in November was proclaimed to be the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Republic_of_China" title="Soviet Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">Soviet Republic of China</a>, an independent Communist-governed state. Although proclaimed Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, Mao's power was diminished, with control of the Red Army being allocated to <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>; Mao meanwhile recovered from <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p77_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p77-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao1931.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Mao1931.jpg/170px-Mao1931.jpg" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Mao1931.jpg/255px-Mao1931.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Mao1931.jpg/340px-Mao1931.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="465" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao1931.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mao in 1931</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Attempting to defeat the Communists, the KMT armies adopted a policy of <a href="/wiki/Encirclement_Campaigns" title="Encirclement Campaigns">encirclement and annihilation</a>; outnumbered, Mao responded with guerrilla tactics influenced by the works of ancient military strategists like <a href="/wiki/Sun_Tzu" title="Sun Tzu">Sun Tzu</a>, but Zhou and the new leadership replaced this approach with a policy of open confrontation and conventional warfare. In doing so the Red Army successfully defeated <a href="/wiki/First_Encirclement_Campaign_against_Jiangxi_Soviet" title="First Encirclement Campaign against Jiangxi Soviet">the first</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Encirclement_Campaign_against_Jiangxi_Soviet" title="Second Encirclement Campaign against Jiangxi Soviet">second encirclements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p78_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p78-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Angered at his armies' failure, Chiang Kai-shek personally arrived to lead the operation; also facing setbacks, he retreated to deal with the <a href="/wiki/Mukden_Incident" title="Mukden Incident">further Japanese incursions into China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p77_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p77-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result of the KMT's change of focus to the defence of China against Japanese expansionism, the Red Army expanded its area of control, eventually encompassing a population of 3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p78_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p78-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao proceeded with his land reform program, in November 1931 announcing the start of a "land verification project" which was expanded in June 1933, also orchestrating education programs and implementing measures to increase female political participation.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Viewing the Communists as a greater threat than the Japanese, Chiang returned to Jiangxi, initiating the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Encirclement_Campaign_against_Jiangxi_Soviet" title="Fifth Encirclement Campaign against Jiangxi Soviet">fifth encirclement campaign</a>, involving the construction of a concrete and barbed wire "wall of fire" around the state, accompanied by aerial bombardment, to which Zhou's tactics proved ineffective. Trapped inside, morale among the Red Army dropped as food and medicine became scarce, and the leadership decided to evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Long_March:_1934.E2.80.931935">The Long March: 1934–1935</span></h3>
<p>On October 14, 1934, the Red Army broke through the KMT line on the Jiangxi Soviet's south-west corner at Xinfeng with 85,000 soldiers and 15,000 party cadres and embarked on the "<a href="/wiki/Long_March" title="Long March">Long March</a>". In order to make the escape, many of the wounded and the ill, as well as women and children, were left behind, defended by a group of guerrilla fighters whom the KMT massacred.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_57_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_57-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The 100,000 who escaped headed to southern Hunan, first crossing the <a href="/wiki/Xiang_River" title="Xiang River">Xiang River</a> after heavy fighting,<sup id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_57_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_57-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> and then the <a href="/wiki/Wu_River_(Yuan_River,_north)" title="Wu River (Yuan River, north)">Wu River</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Guizhou" title="Guizhou">Guizhou</a> where they took <a href="/wiki/Zunyi" title="Zunyi">Zunyi</a> in January 1935. Temporarily resting in the city, they <a href="/wiki/Zunyi_Conference" title="Zunyi Conference">held a conference</a>; here, Mao was elected to a position of leadership, becoming Chairman of <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of China">the Politburo</a>, and <i>de facto</i> leader of both Party and Red Army, in part because his candidacy was supported by Soviet Premier <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>. Insisting that they operate as a guerrilla force, he laid out a destination: the Shenshi Soviet in <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>, Northern China, from where the Communists could focus on fighting the Japanese. Mao believed that in focusing on the anti-imperialist struggle, the Communists would earn the trust of the Chinese people, who in turn would renounce the KMT.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From Zunyi, Mao led his troops to <a href="/wiki/Loushan_Pass" title="Loushan Pass">Loushan Pass</a>, where they faced armed opposition but successfully crossed the river.
